🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Fjords — Carved by glaciers over millions of years. Geirangerfjord and Nærøyfjord are UNESCO heritage. 📚
  • Musk ox — Prehistoric animal surviving in Dovrefjell. Guided safaris available. 📚 📍 Maps
  • White-tailed eagle — Wingspan up to 2.5m! Common along the coast. "Flying doors" the locals call them. 📚
  • Atlantic puffin — Colourful "clown of the sea". Nests on cliffs from May to August. 📚
  • Northern lights — Visible from September to March above the Arctic Circle. 📚

🎵 Music & Art

  • Edvard Grieg — "Peer Gynt" and "In the Hall of the Mountain King" are his masterpieces. 📚
  • Edvard Munch — "The Scream" (1893) is one of the world's most iconic paintings. 📚
  • Stave churches — Wooden Viking-era churches (28 surviving). Unique in the world. 📚
  • a-ha — "Take On Me" (1985). Norway's biggest pop export. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "Who discovered America first: Columbus or the Vikings?" → The Vikings! 500 years earlier! (Leif Erikson, year 1000)

  2. "Why are the fishermen's houses in the Lofoten red?" → Cod liver oil + ochre! (red was the cheapest color)

  3. "Does the sun set in Tromsø in July?" → NO! It's 24 hours of light!

  4. "Bluetooth comes from a Viking king. What was his name?" → Harald Bluetooth! (Blåtand)

  5. "How many Viking wooden churches remain in Norway?" → Only 28! (they had built more than 1000)

  6. "Can you pitch a tent anywhere in Norway?" → YES! It's a right for everyone (Allemannsretten)

  7. "The Norwegian sovereign wealth fund is worth more than..." → $1.7 trillion! Every Norwegian is a "millionaire" on paper.

  8. "How long is Norway's longest fjord?" → 204 km! The Sognefjord \u2014 it would take 2 hours by car to drive along it.

  9. "What is a troll?" → A mountain giant from Norwegian legends! If sunlight hits them, they turn to stone.

  10. "Why do Norwegian houses have grass roofs?" → For insulation! Grass keeps warm in winter and cool in summer. Sometimes goats graze on them!

  11. "How many tunnels are there in Norway?" → More than 1,100! The longest is 24 km \u2014 it takes 20 minutes to drive through!

  12. "What animal can you see in the Lofoten Islands?" → White-tailed eagles! Their wingspan is 2.5 meters \u2014 as wide as dad with arms stretched out!

    What are the Northern Lights? Dancing colored lights in the sky! 🌌 They're caused by particles from the Sun hitting Earth's atmosphere.

    What is a fjord? A long, narrow inlet of sea between tall cliffs! 🏔️ Norway has over 1,000 fjords.

    What is 'brunost'? Brown cheese! 🧀 It's sweet and caramel-flavored, made from whey.

    What is the Midnight Sun? In northern Norway, the sun doesn't set for months in summer! ☀️ In Tromsø, it lasts from May to July.

    What is a troll in Norwegian folklore? A big, ugly creature that lives in mountains and turns to stone in sunlight! 🧌 Many rock formations are said to be 'frozen trolls'.

    What is the Atlantic Road? A road that jumps between islands over the ocean! 🌊 It's one of the most scenic drives in the world.

    How long is Norway's coastline? Over 100,000 km including all fjords and islands! 🏖️ That's more than 2.5 times around Earth.

    What is 'Trollstigen'? The Troll's Ladder! 🧗 It's a mountain road with 11 hairpin turns and a 320m waterfall beside it.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ Wooden trolls — handcrafted, not the Chinese plastic ones!

🏛️ Brunost (brown cheese) — sweet, caramelized. Unique taste. Sliced with a squirrel-shaped cheese slicer (ostehøvel).

🏛️ Marius sweater — the classic Norwegian patterned sweater (expensive but lasts a lifetime)

🏛️ Stockfish — if you like baccalà, buy it directly in the Lofoten

🇩🇰 Denmark (G34-G38)

⏳ Timeline

Period Event Where to see it
793-1066 Viking Age — the Danes conquer England!
965 Harald Bluetooth unifies Denmark and introduces Christianity The Jelling runestones (UNESCO)
1397 Kalmar Union — Denmark governs all Scandinavia
1536 Protestant Reformation
1843 Tivoli opens — the second oldest amusement park in the world 📍 Tivoli Gardens
1913 The Little Mermaid is placed in the port of Copenhagen 📍 The Little Mermaid
1932 Ole Kirk Christiansen invents LEGO in Billund 📍 LEGO House, Billund
1949 Denmark founds NATO
1971 Christiania is born — the "free town" of Copenhagen 📍 Freetown Christiania
2000 The Øresund Bridge opens (Denmark-Sweden)

🧑‍🎨 People to know

Hans Christian Andersen (1805-1875) — The most famous fairy tale writer in the world: The Little Mermaid, The Ugly Duckling, The Snow Queen (which inspired Frozen!), Thumbelina, The Emperor's New Clothes. He was Danish, from Odense. The Little Mermaid statue in the port of Copenhagen is Denmark's most visited monument.

📍 H.C. Andersen Museum, Odense

📍 hcandersen.dk

Ole Kirk Christiansen (1891-1958) — A carpenter from Billund who during the Great Depression started making wooden toys. In 1949 he created the first interlocking plastic bricks. The name LEGO comes from "LEg GOdt" = "play well" in Danish. Today LEGO is the largest toy manufacturer in the world.

📍 LEGO House, Billund — 25 million bricks!

📍 Legoland Billund

📍 legohouse.com

Niels Bohr (1885-1962) — Danish physicist, Nobel Prize 1922. He created the atomic model you study at school (electrons orbiting the nucleus). During WWII, he escaped occupied Denmark hidden in the bomb bay of a plane!

Søren Kierkegaard (1813-1855) — The "father of existentialism". Danish philosopher who wondered "what does it mean to exist?". Too complex for children, but his name is everywhere in Copenhagen.

🏛 What to observe in architecture

🏛️ Nyhavn — the colorful port of Copenhagen. The houses are from the 17th-18th century, painted in bright colors. Andersen lived at numbers 18, 20, and 67!

📍 Nyhavn

🏛️ Tivoli — not just an amusement park: it is a garden with Moorish, Chinese, and Danish architecture mixed. Walt Disney visited it in 1951 and was inspired for Disneyland!

🏛️ Danish design — Denmark is famous for minimalist design. Chairs, lamps, buildings: everything is "simple but perfect". Look for Arne Jacobsen chairs (the "Egg Chair" and the "Swan Chair") in cafés.

🏛️ LEGO House — the building itself is made of giant stacked "bricks". Designed by Bjarke Ingels (the most famous living Danish architect).

🎉 Living traditions in summer

🏛️ Hygge — the Danish concept of "coziness/intimacy". Candles, blankets, coffee, being together. In summer it becomes: picnics in parks, beer at sunset, barbecues with friends.

🏛️ Cykelkultur — Copenhagen has more bicycles than inhabitants! There are bike highways. Children ride alone from age 5.

🏛️ Smørrebrød — the Danish lunch: rye bread with elaborate toppings (salmon, eggs, shrimp). It’s not a simple sandwich — it’s art!

🏛️ Reffen (Copenhagen Street Food) — street food market in containers on the harbor. 40+ kitchens from around the world.

📍 Reffen Copenhagen

🏛️ Sankt Hans Aften (June 23) — bonfires on the beach with a witch doll on top (to "burn evil"). If you are in Denmark on 23/06, look for a bonfire!

🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Wadden Sea — UNESCO heritage. Largest tidal flat system in the world. Millions of migratory birds. 📚
  • Red deer — Denmark's largest wild animal. Common in Jutland forests. 📚
  • Harbour seal — Common along Danish coasts. Can be spotted from beaches. 📚
  • Møns Klint — Dramatic white chalk cliffs. 128m high. Fossils from 70 million years ago! 📚 📍 Maps

🎵 Music & Art

  • Hans Christian Andersen — The Little Mermaid, The Ugly Duckling, The Snow Queen. World's most translated author after the Bible. 📚
  • LEGO — Invented in Billund in 1932. Name from "leg godt" (play well). 📚
  • Danish design — Arne Jacobsen, Hans Wegner. Minimalist furniture that changed the world. 📚
  • Hygge — The Danish art of cosiness. Candles, blankets, hot chocolate. A lifestyle philosophy. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "What does LEGO mean in Danish?" → "Play well!" (LEg GOdt)

  2. "Who wrote The Little Mermaid?" → Hans Christian Andersen! He was Danish, from Odense.

  3. "Frozen is inspired by which Andersen fairy tale?" → The Snow Queen! (1844)

  4. "Walt Disney visited Tivoli and then what did he do?" → He built Disneyland! He was inspired by Tivoli.

  5. "How many LEGO bricks are there in the LEGO House?" → 25 million!

  6. "Bluetooth comes from a Danish king. Which one?" → Harald Bluetooth! (the same as the Vikings)

  7. "How many LEGO bricks exist in the world?" → About 400 billion! If you lined them up they'd reach the Moon 10 times!

  8. "Why are Danes the happiest people in the world?" → They say it's because of "hygge" \u2014 being cozy together with candles, blankets and hot chocolate!

  9. "How old is Tivoli?" → Since 1843! It's one of the world's oldest amusement parks. Walt Disney visited and was inspired to create Disneyland!

  10. "What did Hans Christian Andersen write?" → The Little Mermaid, The Ugly Duckling, The Snow Queen! All the fairy tales you know!

    How many islands does Denmark have? Over 400! 🏝️ But only about 70 are inhabited.

    What toy was invented in Denmark? LEGO! 🧱 The name comes from 'leg godt' meaning 'play well' in Danish.

    What is 'hygge'? A Danish word for cozy togetherness! 🕯️ It means enjoying simple pleasures with loved ones.

    What is the Little Mermaid statue? A bronze statue in Copenhagen harbor! 🧜‍♀️ It's based on Hans Christian Andersen's fairy tale.

    What is a 'smørrebrød'? An open-faced sandwich! 🥪 Danes put all sorts of toppings on dark rye bread.

    What is the Storebælt Bridge? One of the longest bridges in the world! 🌉 It connects two Danish islands and is 18 km long.

    Who wrote 'The Ugly Duckling'? Hans Christian Andersen! 🪶 He was Danish and wrote many famous fairy tales.

    What are Danish pastries called in Denmark? Wienerbroed (Vienna bread)! 🥐 Danes think they came from Austria!

    What is Tivoli? One of the world's oldest amusement parks! 🎢 It opened in Copenhagen in 1843.

    What color is the Danish flag? Red with a white cross! 🇩🇰 It's called the Dannebrog and is the oldest national flag still in use.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ LEGO — in Billund they cost less and there are exclusive sets not sold elsewhere

🏛️ Danish design — a lamp, a cup, a poster (Flying Tiger, HAY, Søstrene Grene)

🏛️ Lakrids by Bülow — gourmet licorice covered in chocolate

🏛️ Smørrebrød to go — in markets, perfect for lunch in the camper

🇩🇪 Germany (G39 — transit via Bremen)

⏳ Timeline

Period Event Where to see it
9th century Charlemagne founds the Holy Roman Empire
1404 The Roland statue in Bremen (symbol of freedom) 📍 Bremen Roland
1810 The Brothers Grimm publish fairy tales The Bremen Town Musicians statue!
1871 German unification under Bismarck
1945 End of WWII, Germany divided
1989 Fall of the Berlin Wall
1990 Reunification

🧑‍🎨 People to know

The Brothers Grimm (Jacob 1785-1863, Wilhelm 1786-1859) — They collected German fairy tales: Cinderella, Snow White, Hansel and Gretel, Little Red Riding Hood, Rapunzel. In Bremen there is the famous statue of the Bremen Town Musicians (donkey, dog, cat, and rooster) — touch the donkey’s paws for good luck!

📍 Bremen Town Musicians statue

🏛 What to observe in architecture

🏛️ Marktplatz of Bremen — the square with the Gothic town hall (UNESCO) and the Roland statue (1404). The town hall has a wine cellar that has served wine continuously for 600 years!

📍 Bremen Rathaus

🏛️ Schnoor — the medieval district of Bremen: alleys 1 meter wide, 15th-century houses, artisan shops.

📍 Schnoor Quarter, Bremen

🎉 Living traditions in summer

🏛️ Bremer Freimarkt is not in summer, but in summer Bremen has the Breminale — a free festival along the Weser river with music, theater, and stalls (in July!)

💡 Germans in summer live in Biergarten (beer gardens) — you can bring your own food and buy only beer!

🏛️ Currywurst at kiosks — the German national fast food (sausage with curry ketchup)

In Bremen: the Ratskeller under the town hall has been serving wine continuously for 600 years (world record!)

🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Wadden Sea (German part) — UNESCO heritage. Seals, migratory birds, tidal flats. 📚
  • White-tailed eagle — Germany's largest bird of prey. Recovering after near-extinction. 📚
  • Bremen Town Musicians — The famous fairy tale! The statue is Bremen's symbol. 📚 📍 Maps

🎵 Music & Art

  • Beethoven — Born in Bonn. Composed his greatest works while going deaf. 📚
  • Brothers Grimm — Collected fairy tales: Cinderella, Snow White, Hansel and Gretel. 📚
  • Bauhaus — Revolutionary art/design school (1919). Changed architecture and design forever. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "The Bremen Town Musicians are 4 animals. Which ones?" → Donkey, dog, cat, and rooster!

  2. "What happens if you touch the donkey's paws?" → It brings good luck! (the statue is shiny where everyone touches)

  3. "Which fairy tale did the Brothers Grimm write?" → Cinderella, Snow White, Little Red Riding Hood... all of them!

  4. "For how many years has the Bremen cellar been serving wine?" → More than 600! (since 1405)

  5. "How many types of bread exist in Germany?" → More than 3,000! Germans are obsessed with bread \u2014 they eat more than anyone else.

  6. "What did Gutenberg invent?" → The printing press! Before him, books were copied by hand \u2014 one could cost as much as a house!

  7. "How long is the German motorway?" → About 13,000 km! And on many sections there's no speed limit!

  8. "Why is Bremen famous?" → For the Town Musicians of Bremen! A donkey, a dog, a cat and a rooster who escape together. But they never actually reached Bremen!

    What is the Autobahn? German highways with (some) sections without speed limits! 🏁 But most sections do have limits now.

    What is a 'Brezel' (pretzel)? A twisted bread snack! 🥨 Its shape is said to represent arms crossed in prayer.

    What is the Black Forest famous for? Cuckoo clocks and Black Forest cake! 🎂 The cake has chocolate, cherries, and whipped cream.

    What is the longest river in Germany? The Rhine! 🌊 It flows 865 km through Germany past castles and vineyards.

    How many federal states does Germany have? 16! 🇺🇳 Each state has its own government and traditions.

    What is 'Currywurst'? A sliced sausage with curry ketchup! 🌭 It was invented in Berlin in 1949 and Germans eat 800 million per year.

    What is the Brandenburg Gate? Berlin's most famous landmark! 🏛️ It was once part of the Berlin Wall border and now symbolizes unity.

    Who invented the printing press? Johannes Gutenberg! 📚 He was German and his invention changed the world in 1440.

    What is 'Neuschwanstein'? A fairy-tale castle in Bavaria! 🏰 Walt Disney used it as inspiration for Sleeping Beauty's castle.

    What is the Miniatur Wunderland? The world's largest model railway! 🚂 It's in Hamburg and has tiny airports, cities, and even a tiny Scandinavia.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ Haribo Goldbären — the original gummy bears (invented in Germany in 1922)

🏛️ Bremer Klaben — traditional Bremen sweet (like panettone with dried fruit)

A magnet of the Bremen Town Musicians — the most iconic souvenir

🇫🇷 France (G40-G42, G50-G53)

⏳ Timeline

Period Event Where to see it
52 BC Julius Caesar conquers Gaul Amiens was a Gallo-Roman city
1137 Construction of Amiens Cathedral begins 📍 Cathédrale d'Amiens
1431 Joan of Arc burned at Rouen
1515 Francis I invites Leonardo da Vinci to France 📍 Clos Lucé, Amboise
1519 Leonardo dies at Clos Lucé (Amboise) Buried in Amboise Castle
1547 Catherine de' Medici receives Chenonceau 📍 Château de Chenonceau
1789 French Revolution
1804 Napoleon becomes Emperor
1889 Inauguration of the Eiffel Tower
1944 D-Day — Normandy landing

🧑‍🎨 People to know

Leonardo da Vinci (1452-1519) — Italian, but died in France! Francis I invited him to Amboise in 1516, giving him Clos Lucé as residence. Leonardo brought the Mona Lisa with him (which never returned to Italy!). At Clos Lucé you can see models of his inventions: the tank, the helicopter, the drawbridge. Kids can touch and operate the machines!

📍 Clos Lucé — Leonardo's machines in the park

📍 Château d'Amboise — where Leonardo is buried

📍 vinci-closluce.com

Catherine de' Medici (1519-1589) — The Italian queen who ruled France. She received Chenonceau and transformed it: added the gallery over the Cher river (the castle's "bridge"). She also introduced the fork to France (before they ate with their hands!).

📍 Chenonceau — ⚠️ Reservation required!

Jules Verne (1828-1905) — The author of Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea, Around the World in 80 Days, Journey to the Center of the Earth. Born in Nantes but lived in Amiens for 34 years! His house is a museum.

📍 Maison de Jules Verne, Amiens

📍 jules-verne.net

🏛 What to observe in architecture

🏛️ Amiens Cathedral — the largest Gothic cathedral in France (200,000 m³!). The facade has 3,000 statues. In summer, a colored light show on the facade (Chroma) displays the original medieval colors.

📍 Cathédrale Notre-Dame d'Amiens

🏛️ Loire Castles — Chenonceau ("castle of the women") is built ON A BRIDGE over the Cher river. 5 arches, 60 meters of gallery over the water. Kids love it because it looks like a fairy tale castle.

🏛️ Hortillonnages d'Amiens — 300 hectares of floating gardens in the city center, cultivated since the Middle Ages. Visited by boat.

📍 Hortillonnages d'Amiens

🏛️ Camargue (Plan B, see Return) — unique landscape: pink salt flats, white horses, black bulls, flamingos. Architecture: the "cabanes de gardians" (white huts with straw roofs shaped like apses).

🎉 Living traditions in summer

🏛️ Marché — every French town has its market 2-3 times a week. Cheese, fruit, bread, rotisserie. The perfect lunch on the road!

14 Juillet (July 14) — National Holiday. Fireworks everywhere! If you are in France on 14/07 (G48 in Plan B), look for a show.

🏛️ Boulangerie — French bread is sacred. Every village has its boulangerie. Baguette tradition (€1.20), pain au chocolat (€1.50), croissant (€1.30). Perfect breakfast!

🏛️ Apéro — the French aperitif: a glass of wine/pastis with olives, chips, saucisson. In summer it’s done everywhere, even in parks.

🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Brittany coast — Pink granite coast, dramatic cliffs, tidal islands. Wild and beautiful. 📚
  • Mont Saint-Michel bay — Tides rise 14m! Fastest tides in Europe. Seals and dolphins. 📚 📍 Maps
  • Atlantic dolphins — Common and bottlenose dolphins visible from the Breton coast. 📚
  • Carnac megaliths — 3,000+ standing stones from 4500 BC. Older than Stonehenge! 📚 📍 Maps

🎵 Music & Art

  • Claude Monet — Father of Impressionism. His water lilies in Giverny are world-famous. 📚
  • Breton music — Celtic roots! Bagpipes (biniou), bombarde, fest-noz dances. Unique in France. 📚
  • Asterix — Comic born in 1959. The indomitable Gauls! Set in Brittany. 📚
  • Jules Verne — Born in Nantes. Father of science fiction. 20,000 Leagues, Around the World in 80 Days. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "Leonardo da Vinci was Italian but died where?" → In France! In Amboise, at Clos Lucé.

  2. "What did Leonardo bring from Italy to France?" → The Mona Lisa! (which never returned to Italy)

  3. "Jules Verne wrote a book about a submarine. What is it called?" → Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea! And he lived in Amiens!

  4. "Chenonceau is a castle built on what?" → A bridge over the river! (the Cher)

  5. "Who brought the fork to France?" → Catherine de' Medici! (an Italian!)

  6. "How many statues does Amiens Cathedral have on its facade?" → 3,000!

  7. "How many different cheeses does France have?" → More than 1,600! One for every day of the year and still some left over!

  8. "How much does the Eiffel Tower weigh?" → 10,100 tons! But if you melted all the iron into its base, it would only be 6 cm tall. The air inside weighs more than the tower!

  9. "Why do the French eat snails?" → Because they're delicious with butter and garlic! They eat 700 million per year!

  10. "What is a croissant?" → A crescent-shaped pastry! Actually the Austrians invented it, but the French made it perfect.

    What is the Eiffel Tower made of? Iron! 🛠️ It has 18,038 iron pieces and 2.5 million rivets.

    What is a 'crêpe'? A very thin pancake! 🥞 French crêpes can be sweet (Nutella, sugar) or savory (ham, cheese).

    How many types of cheese does France produce? Over 1,200! 🧀 There's a different cheese for every day of the year (and then some).

    What is the Tour de France? The world's most famous bicycle race! 🚴 It covers about 3,500 km in 3 weeks.

    What is the Louvre? The world's largest art museum! 🎨 It has the Mona Lisa and over 380,000 objects.

    What is 'bouillabaisse'? A fish stew from Marseille! 🥘 It was originally made by fishermen with the fish they couldn't sell.

    What is Mont Blanc? The highest mountain in Western Europe! 🏔️ It's 4,808 meters high and its name means 'White Mountain'.

    What is the French national motto? Liberté, Égalité, Fraternité! 🇫🇷 It means Liberty, Equality, Brotherhood.

    What is a baguette? A long, thin French bread! 🥖 The French buy about 10 billion baguettes per year.

    What is special about the Basque Country? They speak Basque, a language unrelated to any other! 🗣️ It's one of the oldest languages in Europe.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ Fromage — local cheese (each region has its own!)

🏛️ Baguette tradition — eat immediately, doesn’t last more than 6 hours

🏛️ Confiture (artisan jam) — at markets

🏛️ Savon de Marseille — traditional soap (in Camargue/Provence)

🇪🇸 Spain (G43-G49)

⏳ Timeline

Period Event Where to see it
15000 BC Altamira cave paintings (Cantabria!) Near the Picos de Europa
711-1492 Arab domination (Al-Andalus)
1492 Columbus discovers America + end of Reconquista
1512 The Basque Country joins the Kingdom of Spain (keeping fueros/privileges)
1588 The Invincible Armada is defeated by England
1808-1814 War of Independence against Napoleon
1936-1939 Spanish Civil War Guernica (Gernika) bombed in 1937
1937 Picasso paints Guernica 📍 Gernika Peace Museum
1975 Death of Franco → democratic transition
1997 Opening of the Guggenheim Bilbao — revolutionizes the city 📍 Guggenheim Bilbao

Characters to know

The Basques — The oldest people in Europe! The Basque language (euskera) is not related to ANY OTHER language in the world. No one knows where they come from. They have maintained their identity for thousands of years despite Romans, Visigoths, Arabs, French, and Spaniards.

Basque pelota (jai alai) is the fastest sport in the world (the ball exceeds 300 km/h!)

The Basques invented whaling (12th century) — that’s why the trip includes whale watching!

Pablo Picasso (1881-1973) — Painted Guernica (1937) after the bombing of the Basque city by the Nazis. The painting is at the Reina Sofía in Madrid, but in Gernika (on route G44) there is the Peace Museum with a life-size reproduction.

📍 Gernika Peace Museum

Frank Gehry (1929-) — The Canadian architect who designed the Guggenheim Bilbao (1997). The undulating titanium building transformed Bilbao from a declining industrial city to a world tourist destination. It’s called the "Bilbao effect".

📍 Guggenheim Bilbao

🏛 What to observe in the architecture

🏛️ Guggenheim Bilbao — 24,000 m² of titanium that change color with the light. The giant spider "Maman" by Louise Bourgeois at the entrance (9 meters!). The flower dog "Puppy" by Jeff Koons (12 meters, 70,000 live flowers!). Kids go crazy.

🏛️ Basque Caseríos — traditional farms: large stone houses with gabled roofs, wooden beams. Each family had their caserío for generations.

🏛️ San Juan de Gaztelugatxe — the islet connected to the mainland by a stone bridge with 241 steps. Location of "Dragonstone" in Game of Thrones!

📍 San Juan de Gaztelugatxe

🏛️ Picos de Europa — the most spectacular limestone mountains in Spain. Fuente Dé: cable car that climbs 753 meters in 4 minutes!

🎉 Living traditions in summer

🏛️ Pintxos — the "Basque tapas". Every bar has a counter full of snacks on a skewer. You go from one bar to another (txikiteo), having a pintxo + a glass of txakoli (sparkling white wine). San Sebastián has the highest concentration of Michelin stars per square meter in the world!

🏛️ Fiestas — in summer every pueblo has its patron saint festival with bulls, music, fireworks. In July-August there is almost one every day!

🏛️ Sidrería — in Basque cider houses the cider is poured from the barrel at 2 meters height (txotx!). You eat tortilla de bacalao, chuletón, and Idiazábal cheese.

🏛️ Basque pelota — look for a frontón (pelota court) in any Basque town. Often there are matches in the evening.

🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Picos de Europa — Spain's first national park (1918). Dramatic limestone peaks, chamois, vultures. 📚 📍 Maps
  • Cantabrian brown bear — ~350 bears in the Cantabrian mountains. Recovering population! 📚
  • Griffon vulture — Wingspan up to 2.8m! Common in northern Spain gorges. 📚
  • Atlantic coast — Wild beaches, rías (estuaries), cliffs. Very different from Mediterranean Spain. 📚

🎵 Music & Art

  • Gaita gallega — Galician bagpipes! Celtic roots shared with Scotland and Ireland. 📚
  • Guggenheim Bilbao — Frank Gehry's titanium museum (1997). Transformed the entire city. 📚 📍 Maps
  • Cave of Altamira — 36,000-year-old cave paintings. "Sistine Chapel of Prehistory". 📚
  • Camino de Santiago — 1,000+ year pilgrimage. The scallop shell is the symbol. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "The Guggenheim has a giant dog made of what?" → 70,000 live flowers! It’s called Puppy and is 12 meters tall.

  2. "The Basque language is related to which other language?" → NONE! It is unique in the world. No one knows where it comes from.

  3. "How many steps does San Juan de Gaztelugatxe have?" → 241! (and in Game of Thrones it’s the castle of Dragonstone)

  4. "Basque pelota is the fastest sport in the world. How fast does the ball go?" → More than 300 km/h!

  5. "What are pintxos?" → Snacks on a skewer! You go from one bar to another to eat them.

  6. "How old are the Altamira paintings?" → 17,000! Made by cave men.

  7. "Why do Spaniards eat so late?" → Because Spain uses the wrong time zone! It should have the same as Portugal, but Franco changed it to match Germany.

  8. "What is paella?" → A rice dish with seafood or meat cooked in a giant pan! It comes from Valencia.

  9. "How many castles are there in Spain?" → More than 2,500! The name "Castile" comes from "castles".

  10. "What animal is the symbol of Bilbao?" → A giant dog made of flowers! It's called Puppy and is 12 meters tall, in front of the Guggenheim museum.

    What is a solar eclipse? When the Moon passes between Earth and the Sun! 🌑 For a few minutes, day becomes night.

    What is 'paella'? A rice dish cooked in a big flat pan! 🥘 The original from Valencia has rabbit, chicken, and beans.

    What is flamenco? A passionate Spanish dance with guitar and clapping! 💃 It comes from Andalusia in southern Spain.

    What is the Sagrada Familia? A giant church in Barcelona still being built! ⛪ Gaudí started it in 1882 and it's STILL not finished.

    How many official languages does Spain have? 5! 🗣️ Spanish (Castilian), Catalan, Basque, Galician, and Aranese.

    What is 'tapas'? Small dishes of food shared between friends! 🍽️ The word means 'lids' — bartenders used to cover drinks with a plate of food.

    What is the Camino de Santiago? A famous pilgrimage walk! 🚶 People walk hundreds of km to reach Santiago de Compostela.

    What is 'gazpacho'? A cold tomato soup! 🍅 Perfect for hot Spanish summers — it's served ice cold.

    What is the Running of the Bulls? A festival in Pamplona where bulls run through the streets! 🐂 It happens every July during San Fermín.

    What is the Picos de Europa? A mountain range in northern Spain! 🏔️ The name means 'Peaks of Europe' because they were the first land sailors saw.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ Txakoli — Basque sparkling white wine (for the parents)

🏛️ Idiazábal cheese — smoked, sheep’s milk. Delicious.

🏛️ Boina — the original Basque beret!

🏛️ Anchoas de Santoña — the best anchovies in the world (Cantabria)

🇮🇹 Italy (G51-G53)

⏳ Timeline

Period Event Where to see it
1099 Genoa participates in the First Crusade
1284 Genoa defeats Pisa at Meloria — dominates the Mediterranean
1451 Christopher Columbus is born in Genoa 📍 Columbus House
1528 Andrea Doria makes Genoa an oligarchic republic The Palazzi dei Rolli (UNESCO)
1805 Genoa annexed to the French Empire
1861 Unification of Italy — Genoa is a protagonist (Mazzini, Garibaldi)
1992 Genoa Expo — the Old Port is reborn 📍 Genoa Aquarium

Characters to know

Christopher Columbus (1451-1506) — Genoese! His reconstructed birthplace is near Porta Soprana. He convinced the Spanish Kings to finance the westward voyage. He thought he would reach India — he found America (but died without knowing it!).

📍 Columbus House

📍 Porta Soprana

Andrea Doria (1466-1560) — The admiral who made Genoa "la Superba". Under him, Genoese families built the Palazzi dei Rolli — residences so beautiful they hosted kings and ambassadors (unique system in the world, UNESCO).

📍 Via Garibaldi / Palazzi dei Rolli

Renzo Piano (1937-) — The most famous Genoese architect in the world (Centre Pompidou in Paris, The Shard in London). He redesigned Genoa’s Old Port for Expo 1992, including the Biosphere (the tropical glass bubble on the water).

📍 Biosphere, Old Port

🏛 What to observe in the architecture

🏛️ Caruggi — the alleys of Genoa: the largest medieval historic center in Europe! Alleys 1-2 meters wide, 6-7 floors high. Dark even during the day. Smell of focaccia and pesto.

📍 Via del Campo — the street sung by De André

🏛️ Palazzi dei Rolli (UNESCO) — Via Garibaldi: 3 palace-museums with frescoes, mirrors, and hanging gardens. Palazzo Rosso, Palazzo Bianco, Palazzo Doria-Tursi.

🏛️ Old Port — the old port transformed by Renzo Piano: Aquarium, Biosphere, Galata Maritime Museum, Neptune galleon (reconstruction for Polanski’s film "Pirates").

📍 Neptune Galleon

🏛️ Lanterna di Genova — the oldest working lighthouse in the world (1128!). 77 meters tall.

📍 Lanterna di Genova

🎉 Living traditions in summer

🏛️ Focaccia di Recco — not the normal focaccia! It’s very thin, filled with melted stracchino cheese. You only eat it here. Kids love it.

📍 Manuelina Focacceria, Recco

🏛️ Genovese pesto — the TRUE pesto is made only with basil from Prà (DOP), pine nuts, garlic, Parmesan, Pecorino, EVO oil. Trofie al pesto is the signature dish.

🏛️ Gelato — Genova is one of the capitals of Italian artisanal gelato

🏛️ Stroll — in the evening, the people of Genova walk along the Old Port. Gelato in hand, sea breeze.

🏛️ Ferragosto (August 15) — WARNING: everything is closed! Plan your shopping on the 14th.

💬 Useful words

You are at home! 🇮🇹 But Genovese (zeneize) is a different dialect:

🌿 Nature & Wildlife

  • Cinque Terre NP — Five colourful villages on terraced cliffs. UNESCO heritage. 📚 📍 Maps
  • Dolphins — Bottlenose dolphins common in the Ligurian Sea. Whale watching from Genoa. 📚
  • Mediterranean maquis — Aromatic scrubland: rosemary, lavender, myrtle. Smells incredible! 📚

🎵 Music & Art

  • Paganini — Born in Genoa. The greatest violinist ever. "Devil's violinist". 📚
  • Trallalero — Traditional Genoese polyphonic singing. Male choirs imitating instruments. 📚
  • Fabrizio De André — Genoa's greatest singer-songwriter. "Crêuza de mä" in Genoese dialect. 📚

🎯 Quiz for kids

  1. "Colombo was from which city?" → Genova! His house is near Porta Soprana.

  2. "Where did Colombo think he was going?" → To India! Instead, he found America (but he never knew it).

  3. "How old is the Genova lighthouse (la Lanterna)?" → Almost 900! (since 1128) — the oldest still functioning in the world.

  4. "How wide are the caruggi?" → 1-2 meters! So narrow that a car can't pass through.

  5. "Is the galleon in the port real?" → It's a reconstruction for a movie! (Polanski's Pirates)

  6. "How many types of pasta exist in Italy?" → More than 350! And each region has its favorite shape.

  7. "Why is the Tower of Pisa leaning?" → Because the ground underneath is too soft! They started building it in 1173 and it tilted immediately. It took 200 years to finish!

  8. "How many active volcanoes are there in Italy?" → At least 3 big ones: Etna, Vesuvius and Stromboli! Stromboli erupts every 15 minutes!

  9. "Who invented pizza?" → A pizza maker in Naples in 1889! He made it with tomato, mozzarella and basil for Queen Margherita \u2014 the colors of the Italian flag!

    How many regions does Italy have? 20! 🇮🇹 Each has its own cuisine, dialect, and traditions.

    What is the Colosseum? An ancient Roman arena! 🏟️ It could hold 50,000 spectators watching gladiator fights.

    How many shapes of pasta exist in Italy? Over 350! 🍝 Each region has its own special shapes and sauces.

    What is gelato? Italian ice cream! 🍨 It has less air and fat than regular ice cream, making it denser and creamier.

    What is the Leaning Tower of Pisa? A bell tower that started leaning during construction! 📐 It leans about 4 degrees.

    What did the Romans invent? Roads, aqueducts, concrete, and central heating! 🛣️ Many Roman roads are still used today.

    What is 'la passeggiata'? The Italian evening walk! 🚶 Families stroll through town before dinner — it's a daily tradition.

    What volcano destroyed Pompeii? Mount Vesuvius! 🌋 It erupted in 79 AD and buried the entire city under ash.

    What is the smallest country in the world? Vatican City! 🇻🇦 It's inside Rome and is only 0.44 km².

    What is 'carnevale'? A festival before Lent with masks and costumes! 🎭 Venice's carnival is the most famous with elaborate masks.

    What is the Dolomites? Pink-colored mountains in northern Italy! 🏔️ They turn pink at sunset — it's called 'enrosadira'.

🛍 What to buy

🏛️ Fresh pesto — in vacuum jars it lasts a few days (or buy basil from Prà!)

🏛️ Focaccia di Recco — eat it immediately!

🏛️ Dried trofie — to make trofie with pesto at home

🏛️ Ligurian EVO oil — delicate, perfect for pesto

🍝 Food — Gastronomic Guide

📑 On this page: Table by Country 🇦🇹 Austria 🇨🇿 Czechia 🇵🇱 Poland 🇱🇹🇱🇻🇪🇪 Baltics 🇫🇮 Finland 🇳🇴 Norway 🇩🇰 Denmark 🇩🇪 Germany 🇫🇷 France 🇪🇸 Spain 🇮🇹 Italy 👨‍🍳 Van cooking tips

🍽️ Gastronomy — by Country and Area

Typical dishes, local products and practical tips for eating well while spending little in a van. Focus on foods suitable also for children and easy to find in supermarkets or local markets.

📊 Gastronomy — Table by Country

Country Must-try dishes Budget supermarket Meal budget/4 pax
🇦🇹 Austria Wiener Schnitzel, Kaiserschmarrn, Würstel Hofer, Lidl €20-30
🇨🇿 Czech Republic Trdelník (sweet), Svíčková Lidl, Albert €15-20
🇵🇱 Poland Pierogi, Żurek, Oscypek Biedronka, Lidl €12-18

🇦🇹 Austrian Cuisine (D0-D1)

📜 History of Austrian cuisine

Austrian cuisine is a crossroads of empires: 📚 Wikipedia. The Wiener Schnitzel likely came from Milan (cotoletta alla milanese), brought to Vienna in 1857 by Field Marshal Radetzky. Kaiserschmarrn ("Emperor's mess") was invented for Franz Joseph I when his cook botched a crêpe. Kaffeehäuser (Viennese coffeehouses, 📚 Wikipedia) were born after the Turkish siege of 1683: coffee sacks left by the Turks became a Viennese obsession. Today they're UNESCO heritage. The Sachertorte was created in 1832 by 16-year-old Franz Sacher for Prince Metternich — the original recipe is still secret!

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Tafelspitz — Boiled beef with chive sauce and grated apple. Emperor Franz Joseph's favourite dish. 📚
  • Knödel — Bread dumplings (Semmelknödel) or potato dumplings, served with roast or as sweet apricot-filled dessert (Marillenknödel). 📚
  • Palatschinken — Austrian crêpes filled with apricot jam or Nutella. Perfect for kids!
  • Leberkäse — "Liver cheese" (contains neither liver nor cheese!). Hot meatloaf served in a roll. Classic street food. 📚

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Würstel from Würstelstand — stalls open late (€3-5). Try the Käsekrainer (sausage filled with melted cheese!)
  • Naschmarkt (Vienna) — 120 stalls with food from all over the world. Perfect for lunch (€5-8/person). 📍 Maps
  • Bitzinger Würstelstand — the most famous stall, in front of the Opera (open until 4 am!). 📍 Maps

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Hofer (= Austrian Aldi) — lowest prices. Alpine cheeses (Bergkäse), Tyrolean speck, rye bread, excellent fresh milk etc.
  • Sachertorte — the most famous chocolate cake in the world. The supermarket one is good too (~€4)
  • Heurigen (wine taverns) — in Grinzing or Nussdorf. Cold platters (€15-20 for 4) with local bulk wine

🍳 Van recipes

  • Kaiserschmarrn express — 4 eggs, 200g flour, 200ml milk, butter, powdered sugar. Make a thick omelette, tear it with two forks, sprinkle with sugar. 10 minutes, loved by all!
  • Würstel with Kartoffelsalat — Frankfurter sausages (from Hofer fridge) heated in hot water + potato salad (boil potatoes, season with vinegar/oil/onion/mustard). Classic German dinner in 20 min.
  • Frittatensuppe — hot broth with strips of omelette (make a thin crêpe, roll it and cut into strips, dip in broth). Perfect for cool mountain evenings.

🍽️ To try at the local

  • Wiener Schnitzel — breaded veal cutlet fried in butter. The original is veal, not pork! It should "ripple" when you move it on the plate
  • Kaiserschmarrn — sweet omelette in pieces with powdered sugar and plum compote. Legend: invented for Emperor Franz Joseph!
  • Apfelstrudel — apple strudel with very thin filo pastry. With cream or vanilla ice cream
  • Germknödel — sweet steamed dumpling filled with plum jam, with vanilla sauce and poppy seeds

💡 Tips

  • Würstelstand are open late — perfect for a quick dinner after a late arrival
  • Hofer is the cheapest supermarket (= Aldi). Spar is good but more expensive
  • Tap water in Vienna is alpine spring water — among the best in Europe

🇨🇿 Czech Cuisine (D1-D2, transit)

📜 History of Czech cuisine

Czech cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) is hearty and filling, born to survive long winters. Czech beer has a 1,000-year tradition: Pilsner was invented in Plzeň in 1842 (📚 Wikipedia) — Czechs drink more beer per capita than anyone (140 litres/year!). The Trdelník (chimney cake) seen everywhere in Prague is actually Hungarian/Slovak, but has become the symbol of Prague tourism. Real Czech dishes are knedlíky (boiled bread dumplings) that accompany every meat dish.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Svíčková na smetaně — Beef sirloin with creamy vegetable sauce, cranberries and knedlíky. THE Czech national dish. 📚
  • Vepřo-knedlo-zelo — "Pork-dumplings-sauerkraut": the holy trinity of Czech cuisine. Roast pork, knedlíky and stewed sauerkraut.
  • Kulajda — Creamy porcini mushroom soup with potatoes, dill and poached egg. Perfect comfort food.
  • Koláče — Round pastries filled with poppy seeds, sweet cheese or plum jam. Every grandmother has her own recipe!

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Trdelník — warm chimney cake, sold everywhere in historic centers (~€3). Crunchy and sugary, kids love it
  • Bramboráky — potato pancakes (perfect street food for kids, ~€2-3)

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Lidl/Albert — excellent beer (also non-alcoholic), fresh bread, Hermelin cheeses (Czech Camembert type)
  • Kofola — Czech cola, less sweet than Coca-Cola, unique herbal taste (~€1)

🍳 Van recipes

  • Bramboráky express — grated potatoes + egg + flour + garlic + marjoram + salt. Fry as pancakes in a pan. 15 min, loved by kids!
  • Svíčková express — sliced chicken breast + cream + grated carrot + a spoon of mustard + bay leaf. Simmer 20 min on low heat. Serve with knedlíky (bread dumplings, ready-made in supermarkets) or bread. Perfect Czech comfort food for cool evenings!

🍽️ To try at the local

  • Svíčková — beef in creamy sauce with knedlíky (bread dumplings) and cranberries
  • Vepřo-knedlo-zelo — roast pork with knedlíky and sauerkraut (the national dish)

💡 Tips

  • Only a quick transit (D1-D2) — focus on Trdelník and beer!
  • Czech prices are about half of Italian ones

🇵🇱 Polish Cuisine (D2-D3)

📜 History of Polish cuisine

Polish cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) blends Slavic, Jewish and noble traditions. Pierogi (📚 Wikipedia) are dumplings brought from China via the Silk Road in the 13th century — today they're the national dish. Polish vodka has a 500+ year history (the word "vodka" first appears in a Polish document from 1405!). Bigos ("hunter's stew") improves every time it's reheated — noble families prepared it days before feasts. The Wigilia tradition (Christmas Eve dinner) requires 12 dishes, all meatless.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Bigos — "Hunter's stew": sauerkraut, mixed meats, sausages, dried mushrooms, prunes. Cooked for hours. 📚
  • Żurek — Sour soup of fermented rye flour with sausage and hard-boiled egg. Served inside a bread bowl! 📚
  • Oscypek — Smoked sheep cheese from the Tatra mountains. Spindle-shaped with carved decorations. Grilled and eaten with blueberry jam! 📚
  • Pączki — Polish doughnuts filled with rose jam. On Fat Thursday (Tłusty Czwartek) millions are eaten!

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Oscypek — smoked grilled cheese with blueberry jam. Sold at stalls everywhere (~PLN 10 (~€2.4))
  • Zapiekanka — open baguette with mushrooms, cheese and ketchup. The quintessential Polish street food (~PLN 12-15 (~€2.8–€3.5))
  • Pączki — doughnuts filled with rose jam or cream (the best in Europe!)
  • Gofry — giant waffles with toppings (Nutella, cream, fruit) sold everywhere in summer
  • Bar Mleczny Bambino (Warsaw) — popular canteen from the communist era still active. Pierogi + soup + compote = ~PLN 25 (~€5.9)/person! 📍 Maps
  • Hala Koszyki (Warsaw) — modern food hall with Polish and international cuisine. 📍 Maps

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Biedronka/Lidl — everything costs half of Italy. Stock up for Scandinavia! Buy: pasta, rice, preserves, snacks, Wedel chocolate, juices
  • Frozen Pierogi — supermarket ones are great too (Biedronka has an excellent fresh line, ~PLN 8 (~€1.9))
  • Żubrówka — bison grass vodka (souvenir for adults, ~PLN 30 (~€7))

🍳 Van recipes

  • Pierogi leniwe (lazy pierogi) — 500g ricotta, 1 egg, flour as needed for soft dough. Cut into gnocchi shapes, boil for 3 min, dress with melted butter and breadcrumbs. 15 minutes, loved by children!
  • Placki ziemniaczane — grated potatoes + egg + flour + grated onion + salt. Fry like golden pancakes. Serve with sour cream. 15 min, similar to Czech Bramboráky but thinner.
  • Polish tomato soup — tomato puree + broth + cream + short pasta (or rice). Polish children eat it every week — simple and delicious. 15 min.

🍽️ To try at the local place

  • Pierogi — stuffed ravioli (potato/cheese = "ruskie", meat = "z mięsem", fruit = "z owocami"). In "bar mleczny" cost ~PLN 15-20 (~€3.5–€4.7) for a huge portion!
  • Żurek — sour rye soup with sausage and egg, served in a bread bowl (you also eat the "plate"!)

💡 Tips

  • Stock up for Scandinavia! Polish prices are 50-60% lower than Scandinavian ones. Buy pasta, rice, preserves, snacks
  • Bar Mleczny (dairies) are popular canteens with homemade food at very low prices — look for them everywhere
  • Wedel chocolate is the best in Eastern Europe — buy bars as travel snacks

🇱🇹🇱🇻🇪🇪 Baltic Cuisine (G3-G6)

📜 History of Baltic cuisine

The cuisines of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia (📚 Lithuanian, 📚 Latvian, 📚 Estonian) share common roots: dark rye bread, potatoes, herring, fermented dairy. Dark bread (Rugpjūtis/Rupjmaize) is sacred — throwing it away brings bad luck! Lithuania's farmhouse beer tradition is ancient: unfiltered, unpasteurised beers with recipes passed down for centuries. Estonia has strong Scandinavian influence (herring, salmon), Lithuania more Polish influence (pierogi/cepelinai), Latvia is in between.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Cepelinai (Lithuania) — Giant potato dumplings stuffed with meat, shaped like zeppelins! With sour cream and bacon. 📚
  • Šaltibarščiai (Lithuania) — Cold pink beetroot soup with kefir. Refreshing in summer! 📚
  • Piragi (Latvia) — Crescent-shaped rolls stuffed with bacon and onion. Christmas tradition but available year-round.
  • Verivorst (Estonia) — Blood sausage with barley and spices. Traditional winter dish.
  • Sklandrausis (Latvia) — Rye tart with carrot and potato filling. EU gastronomic heritage.

🌭 Street food / kiosks / take-away

  • Lido (Latvian chain) — self-service with local buffet cuisine. Huge variety, very low prices (~€5-7/person). Locations all over Riga
  • Riga Central Market (Centraltirgus) — in 5 pavilions (former Zeppelin hangars!) smoked fish, black bread, cheeses. Lunch for 4: ~€15-20. 📍 Maps
  • Kibinai — stuffed pastries (specialty of Trakai, Lithuania, ~€2-3 each)

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Maxima/Rimi/Selver — prices similar to Poland. Excellent dairy (sour cream, ricotta)
  • Kohuke (Estonia) — ricotta bars covered in chocolate (perfect snack for kids, ~€0.50!). Buy them by the pack!
  • Black bread — the best in the Baltics, lasts for days. Base of every meal
  • Smoked fish — in refrigerated counters, great and cheap (eel, salmon, sprats)

🍳 Van recipes

  • Šaltibarščiai (Lithuanian pink soup) — cooked grated beets + kefir + diced cucumber + dill + boiled egg. Serve cold. No cooking, perfect for summer, kids love the shocking pink color!
  • Baltic tartines — toasted black bread + butter + smoked fish (sprats or salmon) + red onion + dill. No cooking, lunch in 5 minutes.
  • Kefir with berries — fresh kefir (great and cheap in the Baltics) + blueberries/strawberries + honey. Healthy and quick breakfast or snack.

🍽️ To try at the local place

  • Cepelinai (Lithuania) — giant potato dumplings stuffed with meat (huge portions, ~€5)
  • Šaltibarščiai (Lithuania) — cold pink beet soup (kids find it fun!)
  • Piragi (Latvia) — buns filled with bacon and onion
  • Rupjmaizes kārtojums (Latvia) — black bread dessert with whipped cream
  • Verivorst (Estonia) — blood sausage (for the more adventurous)
  • Olde Hansa (Tallinn) — medieval restaurant in the Old Town. Expensive but unique experience (waiters in costume, candles). Kids go crazy! 📍 Maps

💡 Tips

  • The Baltics have prices similar to Poland — take advantage to stock up before Finland
  • Baltic kefir is excellent and very cheap — use it as a drink/breakfast
  • In covered markets you can have lunch with smoked fish + black bread for ~€3-4/person

🇫🇮 Finnish Cuisine (G6-G14)

📜 History of Finnish cuisine

Finnish cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) is "from forest and lake to table". For centuries Finns lived on fishing, hunting and gathering berries and mushrooms. Kalakukko (fish baked inside a rye bread loaf) is the oldest dish — fishermen carried it as packed lunch. The sauna tradition also influences cuisine: saunapalvikinkku is ham smoked in the sauna for 24 hours! Finns consume more coffee per capita than anyone (12 kg/year!) and more milk than any country. Wild berries (blueberries, arctic cloudberries, lingonberries) are picked by everyone thanks to Jokamiehenoikeus.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Kalakukko — Fish (vendace or perch) baked inside a rye bread crust. Savonia specialty. 📚
  • Karjalanpiirakka — Karelian pasties: rye crust filled with rice porridge, topped with egg butter. National snack! 📚
  • Leipäjuusto — "Bread cheese" — grilled cheese with cloudberry jam (lakka). Squeaky cheese! 📚
  • Lohikeitto — Creamy salmon soup with potatoes and dill. Finnish comfort food par excellence.
  • Mustikkapiirakka — Wild blueberry pie. Finnish blueberries are smaller and more intense than cultivated ones.

🌭 Street food / kiosks / take-away

  • Kauppahalli (covered markets) — every Finnish city has one. Helsinki, Oulu, Rovaniemi. Fresh fish, salmon soups, desserts. Lunch ~€10-12/person. 📍 Oulu Market Hall
  • Karjalanpiirakka — Karelian rice pies with egg butter (typical breakfast, ~€1-2 each, sold everywhere)
  • Grillimakkara — giant grilled sausage (in every picnic area and kiosk, ~€4-5)

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • S-Market/K-Market — prices 30-40% higher than Italy. Excellent fresh salmon (~€12-15/kg). Excellent rye bread
  • Fazer — the blue milk chocolate is iconic (buy as travel snack, ~€2-3)
  • Wild berries — free in the forests! Jokamiehenoikeus (everyman's right) allows picking blueberries, raspberries and mushrooms ANYWHERE, even on private land

🍳 Van recipes

  • Lohikeitto (salmon soup) — fresh salmon cubes + potatoes + carrots + cream + dill. Boil potatoes/carrots 10 min, add salmon 5 min, cream and dill. The perfect dish for cool evenings in Lapland!
  • Pannukakku (Finnish oven pancake) — 3 eggs + 500ml milk + 150g flour + 30g melted butter + 2 tablespoons sugar. Pour into greased pan, cover and cook on medium-low heat 15 min. Serve with jam and cream. Sunday breakfast!
  • Nordic salmon pasta — fresh salmon cubes + cream + dill + lemon + short pasta. The wildcard dish that works all over Scandinavia. 15 min.

🔥 Grill

  • Picnic areas/Laavu — covered structures with fireplaces in the woods are free and everywhere. Bring grillimakkara (sausages) and bread
  • Grillimakkara on fire — Finnish tradition: giant sausage on a stick, grilled over the laavu fire. Kids love the ritual
  • Firewood — in national parks and recreational areas managed by Metsähallitus firewood is provided free (piles next to the structure). Just bring fire starters/matches!

🍽️ To try at the local place

  • Kalakukko — bread filled with fish (specialty of Kuopio)
  • Mustikkapiirakka — blueberry pie (pick blueberries for free in the woods!)
  • Lohikeitto — creamy salmon soup (found in every restaurant/kauppahalli)

💡 Tips

  • Berry picking is a perfect activity for kids — "blueberry hunting" in the woods!
  • Filter coffee is free in many shops and service stations (Finns drink the most coffee per capita in the world!)
  • Finnish picnic areas almost always have free public grills (laavu/kota) — buy sausages and grill!
  • Taps water is excellent everywhere

🇳🇴 Norwegian Cuisine (G14-G33)

📜 History of Norwegian cuisine

Norwegian cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) is shaped by fjords and extreme climate. Vikings invented preservation: dried fish (tørrfisk/stockfish), smoked (røkelaks) and fermented (rakfisk). Stockfish (📚 Wikipedia) dried in the Lofoten Islands was Viking "currency" — exported across Europe (including Italy for baccalà!). Brunost (brown cheese) was invented in 1863 by a farm girl, Anne Hov, who had the idea of adding cream to whey. Today it's the national cheese. Norwegian salmon is the world's most exported fish — salmon sushi was "invented" by Norwegians who convinced the Japanese in the 1980s!

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Brunost — Sweet brown whey cheese. Cut in thin slices with the ostehøvel (cheese slicer, a Norwegian invention!). 📚
  • Fårikål — Lamb and cabbage stew. Norwegian national dish. Simple but delicious. 📚
  • Rømmegrøt — Sour cream porridge with melted butter, sugar and cinnamon. Mountain farm tradition.
  • Svele — Norwegian pancakes served on ferries! With butter and sugar. Ferry tradition.
  • King Crab (Kongekrabbe) — Giant crab from the north (legs up to 1.5m!). Eaten fresh in Tromsø and Finnmark. 📚

🌭 Street food / kiosks / take-away

  • Svele — Norwegian pancake (sold on ferries, ~NOK 30 (~€2.8)). The quintessential "ferry snack"
  • Bakeri (bakeries) — kanelboller (cinnamon buns) and skillingsboller, perfect snack (~NOK 35-45 (~€3.2–€4.2))
  • Ferries — Svele + coffee at reasonable prices. Every crossing = snack!

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Brunost — sweet brown cheese (caramel flavor, kids love it on bread!)
  • Fiskekaker — fish cakes (easy to heat, ~NOK 40)
  • Røkelaks — smoked salmon (top quality, ~NOK 80-120 (~€7.4–€11))
  • Fresh salmon (~NOK 150-200/kg (~€14–€19)) — superior quality to any Italian restaurant. Cook in the van!
  • Rema 1000 "Middag for en hundrings" — ready meals for 4 at NOK 100 (~€9.3) (special series)
  • Rema 1000/Kiwi — the cheapest supermarkets. Avoid Joker and Meny (expensive)

🍳 Van recipes

  • Nordic salmon — salmon fillet with salt/pepper/dill, cook in pan 4 min per side. Serve with boiled potatoes and pickled cucumber. The dish you will eat most often!
  • Fiskekaker in pan — fish cakes (from supermarket) heated in pan with butter + salad + bread. Dinner in 5 minutes, kids like it.
  • Salmon and cream pasta — fresh salmon cubes + cream + dill + pasta. The Norwegian wildcard dish. 15 min.
  • Fiskesuppe (fish soup) — diced cod/salmon + potatoes + carrots + cream + mild curry. Similar to Lohikeitto but with curry. Perfect after a rainy day.

🔥 Grill

  • Grillhytte — free barbecue huts in many campsites and rest areas. Bring sausages and bread!
  • Firewood — not always provided. Often available at campsites; in remote areas bring charcoal/briquettes or buy a bag of firewood at the gas station (~NOK 50-80). Always keep a supply in the van!

🍽️ To try at the local spot

  • Raspeball/Komle — potato dumplings (west coast, traditional Thursday dish)
  • Vafler — heart-shaped waffles with sour cream and jam (in every café)
  • Bacalao — stockfish (Lofoten = world capital!)
  • Krabbe — king crab (if you find a fisherman, unbeatable price)
  • Fiskebrygga (fishermen's piers) — in Tromsø, Bergen, Svolvær. Fish soup ~NOK 120-150 (~€11–€14)

💡 Tips

  • ⚠️ A restaurant meal for 4 in Norway easily costs €80-120. Cooking in the van is almost mandatory!
  • "10 for 100 kr" offers on fruit and vegetables at Kiwi and Rema 1000
  • Tap water excellent everywhere — often better than bottled water
  • On ferries they sell Svele and coffee — it's the travel snack
  • Bring pasta and rice from Italy (or buy in Poland) — costs double here

🇩🇰 Danish Cuisine (G33-G38)

📜 History of Danish cuisine

Danish cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) has undergone a revolution: from traditional smørrebrød (open sandwiches) to René Redzepi's "New Nordic" (Noma, 4-time world's best restaurant). Smørrebrød (📚 Wikipedia) originated in medieval times: rye bread was the "plate" on which food was placed. Danish pastries (wienerbrød) were actually brought by Austrian bakers in 1850 during a Danish bakers' strike! Carlsberg was founded in 1847 and its laboratory discovered pure yeast for lager beer — giving the discovery to the world for free.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Smørrebrød — Open sandwiches on rye bread: pickled herring, roast beef, shrimp eggs. A culinary art! 📚
  • Frikadeller — Danish meatballs of pork and veal, fried in butter. With potatoes and parsley sauce. 📚
  • Flæskesteg — Roast pork with crispy crackling. Christmas dish but available year-round in sandwiches (flæskesteg sandwich).
  • Rødgrød med fløde — Red berry compote with cream. The name is impossible to pronounce for non-Danes (Danish test!).
  • Pølsevogn — Danish hot dog cart. The "ristet" (grilled) with remoulade, fried and crispy onions is the classic.

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Pølse — Danish hot dog from red stalls (with pickles and fried onions, ~DKK 40 (~€5.4)). The "ristet hotdog med det hele" is the full version
  • Pølsevogn (red stalls) — the cheapest lunch option for families (~DKK 160 (~€21) for 4 hot dogs)
  • Torvehallerne (Copenhagen) — the nicest food hall. Gourmet Smørrebrød, fresh juices, chocolate. Lunch ~DKK 100-150 (~€13–€20)/person. 📍 Maps
  • Grød — gourmet porridge chain (modern Danish breakfast, ~DKK 65 (~€8.7)). Also savory versions!
  • Softice — soft serve ice cream sold everywhere in summer (~DKK 30 (~€4)) — kids will ask for it every day!

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Netto/Lidl/Rema 1000 — prices 40-50% higher than Italy but less than Norway
  • Rugbrød — dark rye bread (base of every Danish meal, lasts 5-7 days). Always buy some!
  • Lurpak — the most famous Danish butter in the world (excellent and relatively cheap here)
  • Lagkagehuset — the most beloved bakery. Croissants, kanelsnegle (cinnamon rolls), fresh rugbrød

🍳 Van recipes

  • DIY Smørrebrød — rugbrød + butter + smoked salmon (or eggs/cheese/ham) + dill + lemon. No cooking, perfect lunch in 5 minutes!
  • Æbleskiver in pan — 250g flour + 2 eggs + 300ml buttermilk + 1 tsp baking soda + sugar. Cook like small round pancakes in a pan with butter. Serve with powdered sugar and jam. The quintessential Danish snack!
  • Rugbrød with scrambled eggs — toasted rye bread + creamy scrambled eggs + chives + smoked salmon. Danish breakfast in 5 min.

🍽️ To try at the local spot

  • Smørrebrød — open sandwiches with elaborate toppings (try at Torvehallerne)
  • Æbleskiver — spherical pancakes with powdered sugar (kids go crazy for them!)
  • Flæskesteg — roast pork with crispy crackling (the national dish)

💡 Tips

  • At Legoland Billund bring a packed lunch — internal restaurants are very expensive
  • In Denmark dinner is early (18:00-19:00) — perfect times for kids!
  • Rugbrød is the base of everything — always buy a supply
  • Pølsevogn (red stalls) are everywhere and are the cheapest option for families

🇩🇪 German Cuisine (G39 — Bremen transit)

📜 History of German cuisine

German cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) varies enormously by region. Bremen, a Hanseatic city, has a maritime tradition: herring, smoked eel, Labskaus (sailors' stew). The Reinheitsgebot (📚 Wikipedia) of 1516 is the world's oldest beer purity law: only water, malt, hops and yeast. Germany has 1,500+ breweries and 5,000+ different beers! Brot (German bread) is UNESCO heritage: over 3,000 registered varieties, more than any other country.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Labskaus (Bremen) — Pink stew of corned beef, beetroot, potatoes with fried egg and herring. Hanseatic sailors' dish! 📚
  • Bremer Knipp — Oat and spiced meat sausage, fried and served with pickles. Bremen local specialty.
  • Franzbrötchen (Hamburg/Bremen) — Cinnamon and butter pastry. The German croissant! Perfect for breakfast.
  • Fischbrötchen — Roll with pickled herring (Matjes), onion and gherkin. Northern street food! 📚

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Currywurst — sliced sausage with curry ketchup sauce and fries. The national fast food, invented in Berlin in 1949. Kids love it! (~€4-5)
  • Brezel (Pretzel) — knot-shaped bread, crunchy outside and soft inside, sprinkled with coarse salt. Perfect travel snack (~€1-2)
  • Bratwurst — grilled sausage in a bun (Brötchen). Each region has its own variant (~€3-4)
  • Fischbrötchen — fish sandwich (marinated herring, salmon or shrimp) typical of the north. At Bremen port ~€4-5

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Aldi/Lidl/Rewe — some of the lowest prices in Western Europe. Excellent fresh bread (Vollkornbrot = whole rye)
  • Kartoffelsalat — ready potato salad (north version: with mayonnaise; south: with vinegar and oil)
  • Apfelschorle — apple juice with sparkling water, the national drink (~€1)
  • Beer — great at ~€0.80. Endless varieties

🍳 Van recipes

  • Currywurst express — sausages (Bratwurst) grilled in a pan, sliced. Sauce: ketchup + curry powder + paprika. Serve with bread or fries. 10 minutes, loved by all!
  • DIY Fischbrötchen — fresh buns + marinated herrings (from the fridge counter) + onion + pickles. No cooking, lunch in 3 minutes.
  • Kartoffelsuppe — diced potatoes + broth + sliced sausages + cream + chives. Hearty soup in 20 min.

🍽️ To try at the local spot

  • Bremer Knipp — Bremen specialty: oat and meat patty, fried in butter (if you find a traditional place)

💡 Tips

  • Bremen is just a transit (G39) — stock up at the German supermarket for the following days in France. German prices are much lower!
  • German bread is the best in Europe — buy Vollkornbrot (lasts days) for the trip

🇫🇷 French Cuisine (G39-G42, G50-G51)

📜 History of French cuisine

French cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) has been UNESCO heritage since 2010. Auguste Escoffier (📚 Wikipedia) codified modern cuisine in 1903 with "Le Guide Culinaire". The baguette (📚 Wikipedia) became UNESCO heritage in 2022 — the French consume 10 billion per year! The fromage (cheese) tradition counts 1,200+ varieties — De Gaulle said: "How can you govern a country with 246 different cheeses?". The croissant is actually Austrian (Kipferl), brought to Paris in 1838. Brittany and Normandy (on your route) are famous for crêpes, cider, salted butter and oysters.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Breton crêpes — Buckwheat galettes (savoury) and wheat crêpes (sweet). With cider! 📚
  • Moules-frites — Mussels in white wine with fries. Classic Atlantic coast dish. 📚
  • Camembert — Soft cheese from Normandy. The real one is "au lait cru" (raw milk). 📚
  • Kouign-amann — Breton pastry of butter, butter and more butter. Crispy outside, soft inside. Paradise!
  • Cidre — Breton/Norman apple cider. Sweet (doux) or dry (brut). Drunk from "bolées" (ceramic cups). 📚

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Baguette + fromage — the perfect combo (fresh baguette every morning in boulangerie, ~€1.20!)
  • Marchés (markets) — every city has at least one, 2-3 times a week. Fruit, cheeses, rotisserie (roast chicken ~€8 whole!), olives, bread. The perfect lunch
  • Boulangeries — fresh baguette (€1.20) + cheese + ham = lunch for 4 under €10
  • Crêperies — galette complète (ham/cheese/egg) ~€7-9. Also take-away!

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Intermarché/Leclerc — the cheapest (better than Carrefour). Extraordinary cheeses at €2-4, fresh baguette, excellent wine at €3-5
  • Quiche Lorraine — ready savory tart (~€3-4 per portion)
  • Fromage de chèvre — goat cheeses from the Loire are among the best in the world (Sainte-Maure, Valençay, Crottin de Chavignol, ~€2-4)
  • Loire wines — Vouvray (sweet white), Chinon (light red), Crémant de Loire (sparkling, €5-8!)
  • Pain au chocolat — for kids' breakfast (~€1.20)

🍳 Van recipes

  • Croque-monsieur express — sliced bread + ham + gruyère + béchamel (or just butter). In pan with lid 3 min per side. Dinner in 10 minutes, adored by kids!
  • Van salade niçoise — canned tuna + boiled eggs + tomatoes + olives + green beans + potatoes. No cooking (except eggs), fresh and complete lunch.
  • Ratatouille express — zucchini + eggplant + peppers + diced tomatoes, all in pan with oil and garlic, 20 min on medium heat. Serve with baguette. The dish that tastes of Provence!
  • Tartine au chèvre — baguette + goat cheese + honey + walnuts. Aperitif/light dinner in 2 minutes.

🍽️ To try at the local spot

  • Crêpes — both sweet (Nutella, sugar-lemon) and savory (galettes)
  • Moules-frites — mussels and fries (Atlantic coast)
  • Rillettes de Tours — spreadable pork cream (Loire area, on bread = perfect aperitif)
  • Tarte Tatin — upside-down apple tart (invented by mistake in Lamotte-Beuvron in the Loire!)

💡 Tips

  • France is the motorhome cook's paradise — cheese, bread, wine at unbeatable prices
  • Buy wine directly from the caves (cellars) along the Loire — free tasting and unbeatable prices
  • The pain au chocolat is called "chocolatine" in the southwest — don't make the mistake!
  • Morning markets have fruit/vegetables/cheese at better prices than supermarkets

🇪🇸 Spanish Cuisine (D43-D49)

📜 History of Spanish cuisine

Spanish cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) of the north is very different from Mediterranean. The Basque Country has the highest concentration of Michelin stars in the world! Pintxos (📚 Wikipedia) are Basque culinary art: mini gastronomic creations on bread, fixed with a toothpick. You go from bar to bar ("txikiteo"). Asturian cider (📚 Wikipedia) is poured from a metre high ("escanciar") to oxygenate it! The Camino de Santiago created a tradition of "menú del peregrino" (3 courses + wine for ~12€) along the entire north.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Basque pintxos — Mini gastronomic masterpieces. The best: gilda (anchovy+olive+chilli), txangurro (crab), croquetas. San Sebastián is the world capital. 📍 Maps Parte Vieja
  • Fabada asturiana — Stew of giant white beans with chorizo, morcilla and bacon. Spain's heartiest dish! 📚
  • Pulpo a la gallega — Boiled octopus with paprika, oil and coarse salt on wood. Galician specialty. 📚
  • Tarta de Santiago — Almond cake with the Santiago cross in powdered sugar. No flour! 📚
  • Asturian cider — Apple cider poured from height (escanciar). Drunk in one gulp! Sidrerías in Oviedo and Gijón.

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Pintxos — snacks on bread (San Sebastián = world capital! ~€2-3 each). The ritual: enter a bar, take 1-2 pintxos + txakoli, pay, move to the next bar
  • Tortilla española — potato omelette (at the bar ~€2 per portion, perfect for children)
  • Churros con chocolate — for breakfast or snack (~€4 for 4 people!)
  • Croquetas — creamy croquettes (ham or cod, ~€1-2 each)
  • Pintxos bar crawl (San Sebastián, Parte Vieja) — budget: ~€30-40 for 4 people if you do 3-4 bars! 📍 Maps
  • Mercado de la Ribera (Bilbao) — the largest covered market in Europe. Pintxos on the upper floor with river view. 📍 Maps

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Mercadona/Lidl/Dia — prices similar or lower than Italy. Excellent ready meals in the fridge section (tortilla, croquetas, ensaladilla) at €2-4
  • Jamón ibérico — sliced ham (~€3), much cheaper than in Italy
  • Gazpacho — cold soup in a bottle (Alvalle or Mercadona brand, ~€2/liter). Perfect for the motorhome in summer, zero cooking!
  • Fruit — excellent and cheap (peaches, watermelons, melons)

🍳 Motorhome recipes

  • Tortilla española — 4 thinly sliced potatoes, fried in plenty of oil, then 6 beaten eggs. Cook on low heat for 10 min, flip with a plate, another 5 min. Eaten hot or cold — lasts 2 days! The wildcard dish of the trip in Spain
  • Fresh gazpacho — ripe tomatoes + pepper + cucumber + garlic + oil + vinegar + stale bread. Blend everything. Serve cold. Zero cooking, refreshing with 35°C!
  • Pan con tomate — toasted bread + rubbed tomato + oil + salt + jamón. Spanish breakfast in 3 minutes. Kids love it!
  • Motorhome patatas bravas — diced potatoes fried in a pan + brava sauce (ketchup + tabasco + smoked paprika + garlic). Hot tapa in 15 min.

🍽️ To try at the restaurant

  • Pulpo a la gallega — Galician-style octopus (with paprika and oil)
  • Asadores (Castile) — restaurants specialized in wood-fired roasts. Lechazo (lamb) and cochinillo (suckling pig) — huge portions to share
  • Fabada asturiana — bean stew (Asturias)
  • Cachopo — giant breaded cutlet stuffed with ham and cheese (Asturias)
  • Sidra natural — Asturian cider poured from above ("escanciar")

💡 Tips

  • In Spain, dinner is late (9:00 PM+). For children, have a "merienda" (substantial snack at 6:00 PM) with tortilla/churros and then a light dinner
  • The menú del día (fixed lunch) costs €10-14 and includes first course + second course + dessert + drink + bread. The best deal in European dining!
  • Spanish children eat croquetas everywhere — they are the local "meatballs"
  • Mercadona has excellent ready meals in the fridge section — perfect for lazy evenings

🇮🇹 Italian Cuisine — Return (D50-D53)

📜 History of Ligurian cuisine

Ligurian cuisine (📚 Wikipedia) is "poor cuisine" turned gourmet. Pesto genovese (📚 Wikipedia) descends from Roman "moretum" (garlic pounded with cheese), evolved with Genoese DOP basil — smaller and sweeter than common basil. Focaccia genovese (📚 Wikipedia) is eaten for breakfast dipped in cappuccino! Farinata (📚 Wikipedia) was invented by accident: during a storm, barrels of chickpeas and oil spilled in the hold — the mixture baked by the sun became a delicacy. Genoa was "La Superba" of the Maritime Republics: spices, salted anchovies, and maritime trade shaped the cuisine.

🍽️ More dishes to try

  • Trofie al pesto — Hand-rolled fresh pasta with pesto, potatoes and green beans. THE Genoese dish. 📚
  • Focaccia di Recco — Two ultra-thin layers with melted stracchino inside. IGP certified. Different from classic focaccia! 📚
  • Monterosso anchovies — Salted or fried. The Cinque Terre have been famous for anchovies since the 13th century.
  • Cima alla genovese — Stuffed veal pocket with eggs, peas, pine nuts. Served cold in slices. Festive dish. 📚
  • Sciacchetrà — Passito wine from Cinque Terre. Produced in tiny quantities on terraces overlooking the sea. 📚

🌭 Street food / stalls / take-away

  • Focaccia genovese — thin, oily, crispy outside and soft inside. The best in Italy. In downtown bakeries ~€2-3 per portion
  • Farinata — very thin chickpea flour cake baked in a wood oven. Crispy at the edges, soft in the center. Ligurian specialty for 800 years (~€3-4)
  • Panissa — chickpea flour fritters (cousin of farinata, but fried in sticks)
  • Mercato Orientale MOG (Via XX Settembre 75R) — covered market with street food + fresh products. Lunch for 4: ~€25-30. 📍 Maps
  • Friggitoria Carega (Vico Carega 14R) — mixed fried take-away, cone ~€8

🛒 To buy at the supermarket

  • Pesto alla genovese — the real pesto (DOP basil, pine nuts, Parmesan, Fiore Sardo). Buy an artisanal jar at Mercato Orientale as a gastronomic souvenir!

🍳 Motorhome recipes

  • Trofie al pesto — typical Genoese pasta (short, twisted) with fresh pesto, potatoes, and green beans. The dish that marks the return home! 15 min.
  • Last-minute pesto pasta — any short pasta + fresh pesto from Mercato Orientale + a drizzle of oil. The simplest and best dinner after 50 days of travel.

🍽️ To try at the restaurant

  • Mixed fried seafood — calamari, anchovies, shrimp. At the old port ~€10-12 per portion
  • Antica Sciamadda (Via San Giorgio 14R) — farinata + panissa since 1700! Portions ~€3-5. Institution. 📍 Maps

💡 Tips

  • After 50+ days of foreign cuisines, focaccia genovese will be the best "welcome back to Italy" possible!
  • Trofie al pesto with potatoes and green beans — the quintessential Ligurian dish, not to be missed before going home

🍽️ Gastronomy — Motorhome Cooking Tips

Tip Detail
Stock from Italy Pasta, rice, EVO oil, moka coffee, basic spices. They cost twice as much in Scandinavia!
Universal wildcard dish Fresh salmon pasta (works in all Nordic countries, fresh salmon everywhere)
Typical breakfast Local bread + cheese + fruit. In Scandinavia: Karjalanpiirakka/Brunost + coffee
Quick lunch Smørrebrød/tartines with leftovers from the night before. Zero cooking, zero gas!
Typical dinner Barbecue in picnic areas (Finland/Norway) or pasta/soup in the motorhome
Water Drinkable from the tap in ALL 13 countries! Fill water bottles everywhere
Wild berries Free in the forests of Finland and Norway (Jokamiehenoikeus/Allemannsretten)
Markets Prefer local markets over supermarkets for fresh fruit/vegetables/cheese

🚐 Camping — Rules by Country

Country Rule Notes
🇳🇴 Norway ✅ Allemannsretten (right of public access) Free camping OK >150m from dwellings, max 2 nights same spot
🇫🇮 Finland ✅ Jokamiehenoikeus Like Norway: free camping OK >150m, max 2 nights
🇩🇰 Denmark ❌ Forbidden Only in campsites/stopover areas. Exception: 800+ free "shelters"
🇩🇪 Germany ❌ Forbidden Only campsites. 1 night tolerated in remote areas
🇫🇷 France ⚠️ Regulated Forbidden in many coastal areas. Tolerated in remote areas
🇪🇸 Spain ⚠️ Regulated Forbidden in many areas. Tolerated in remote non-coastal areas
🇮🇹 Italy ❌ Forbidden Only stopover areas and campsites
🇦🇹 Austria ⚠️ Tolerated 1 night outside towns (not in natural parks!)
🇨🇿 Czech Republic ❌ Forbidden Only authorized campsites. Crossing in first 2 days
🇵🇱 🇱🇹 🇱🇻 🇪🇪 ⚠️ Grey area Generally tolerated outside towns

Recommended apps: Park4Night, iOverlander

🥾 Trekking — Trails for Families and Solo

Divided into 👨‍👩‍👧‍👦 With kids (easy trails, max 2-3h, suitable for 6-8 years old) and 🏃 Solo/Advanced (start at dawn, return for breakfast/lunch before kids wake up).

🌟 Top 5 — Solo (dawn start)

# Trek Day Duration Elevation gain Why
1 Segla (Senja) D16 3-4h R/T 639m Cliff overlooking Mefjorden. Spectacular.
2 Reinebringen (Lofoten) D21 2h 45m–3h 30m R/T 480m 1986 Sherpa steps. Iconic view of Reine. Start at 5:00 = summit only.
3 Ryten + Kvalvika (Lofoten) D22 3-4h R/T 460m Hidden beach viewed from above.
4 Vidden Trail (Bergen) D30 5-7h 400m Ulriken-Floyen crossing, 15 km at altitude.
5 Ruta del Cares (Picos) D45 7–8h R/T 300m "Divine" gorge, 12 km one-way. Start at 6:00 from Poncebos.

🌟 Top 5 — With children

# Trek Day Duration Difficulty Why
1 Offersøykammen (Lofoten) D20 1h 30m R/T Easy-moderate View of bridges and beaches, short but wow.
2 Fløyen Troll Forest (Bergen) D30 1h Easy Cable car + magical path with wooden trolls.
3 Preikestolen (Stavanger) D32 5-6h R/T 350m, moderate The classic. Feasible with children 6+. No railing!
4 San Juan de Gaztelugatxe (Basque Country) D44 1h 30m R/T Easy 241 steps, GoT's "Dragonstone".
5 Fuente Dé at altitude (Picos) D45 1h Easy Cable car at 1,800m + panoramic walk.

Trek Type Duration Notes

Lagos de Covadonga 👨‍👩‍👧‍👦 1h 30m 5 km, mountain lakes, easy
