Naranjo de Bulnes viewpoint 🏃 4-5h round trip From Pandebano. Moderate-difficult.

🥾 Trailhead: 📍 Fuente Dé cable car 📍 Lagos de Covadonga 📍 Ruta del Cares (Poncebos)

🎯 Practical Tips

🥾 Arctic Norway sunrise start (G15-G23): the sun never sets! "Sunrise" doesn’t exist, but starting at 4:00-5:00 guarantees empty trails.

🥾 Preikestolen with children: start by 7:00, bring snacks, poles, and patience. Many families do it successfully (6+ years). The 6-year-old might struggle on the last stretch: allow extra time. ⚠️ No railing at the top: hold little ones’ hands.

🥾 Ruta del Cares: DO NOT bring children under 12 years (cliffs without protection, narrow path). Start at 6:00 from Poncebos, return by lunch.

🥾 Minimum gear: light hiking boots (not sneakers!), telescopic poles, rain jacket, energy snacks, 1L water.

🥾 Useful app: AllTrails for offline GPS tracks.

🏔️ Mountain Preparation and Safety

Essential gear for family:

Item For whom Why
Waterproof hiking boots Everyone Wet trails in Norway/Picos. NO sneakers!
Telescopic poles Adults + 8-year-old child Reduce knee strain by 25% downhill
Light rain jacket Everyone Weather changes within 10 minutes in Norway
Fleece Everyone Cold at altitude even in July (5-10°C)
20L backpack with 1.5L water Adults Bring energy snacks every 45 min for kids
Emergency thermal blanket 1 per family Weighs 50g, can save lives
Whistle Children If separated: 3 whistles = SOS
Powerbank + charged phone Adults Offline GPS, emergency

Golden rules with children 6-8 years:

  1. Never exceed 3h of actual walking (5-6h with breaks)

  2. Snack every 45 minutes — hunger = crying and refusal to walk

  3. Gamification: count bridges, look for animals, "who reaches the rock first?"

  4. Always have Plan B: if the child collapses, turn back without drama

  5. Early start: less heat, fewer people, more motivation

Specific dangers by area:

🥾 Norway (Preikestolen, Reinebringen): NO railing on cliffs. Hold children’s hands in the last 100m. Sudden strong wind.

🥾 Picos de Europa (Ruta del Cares): narrow path with cliff drop. NO children <12 years.

🥾 Lofoten: trails often muddy/slippery. Residual snow possible up to mid-July at altitude.

🥾 Finland: flat terrain but aggressive mosquitoes (DEET 30%+ mandatory G8-G15)

Weather and decisions:

Check Yr.no the night before

If rain >60% → rain plan (see ☔ Rain Plan)

If wind >50 km/h → NO ridge trek (Segla, Reinebringen, Vidden)

Thick fog → only marked trails with cairns (Norway has almost all)

🎣 Fishing — Licenses and Spots by Country

Fishing with children is one of the most relaxing and rewarding activities of the trip. Here's what you need country by country.

📋 Fishing — License Summary

Country Sea fishing Freshwater fishing Children Where to buy
🇫🇮 Finland N/A (lakes) State fee €6/day or €16/week + local permit Free <18 eraluvat.fi
🇳🇴 Norway FREE License from owner + salmon fee Free <16 elveguiden.no (salmon)
🇩🇰 Denmark Fishing license DKK 46/day (~€6) Fishing license + local permit Free <18 fisketegn.dk
🇩🇪 Germany ⚠️ Complicated Not recommended (exam required) — —
🇫🇷 France FREE (shore) Fishing card ~€15/day Free <12 cartedepeche.fr
🇪🇸 Spain ⚠️ Mandatory license ~€43/3 years Regional license ~€10-15/day Free <14 fishinglicensespain.com
🇮🇹 Italy FREE (shore) Type B license Free —

📍 Fishing — Details by Area

🇫🇮 Finland (G7–G15)

Finland is a fishing paradise. 188,000 lakes, very clean waters, and a simple licensing system.

What to fish: pike (hauki), perch (ahven), whitefish (siika), lake trout (taimen), Arctic char (nieriä in Lapland).

Tip for kids: fishing with mato-onki (fixed rod with float and worm) is completely free for everyone in Finland, no license needed. Just a 3-4m rod, a float, and worms. Guaranteed perch!

Best spots on the route:

🎣 D7-G8 Lake Saimaa: Finland's largest lake. Pike and perch from any pier.

🎣 D12 Rovaniemi: Kemijoki river (salmon running in July — special local permit required).

🎣 D13 Lake Inari: lake trout and Arctic char. Local permit ~€10/day on eraluvat.fi.

🎣 D14 Kilpisjärvi: Arctic char. Permit ~€8/day at visitor center.

Recommended gear: 2.4m telescopic rod + small reel + 5-10g spinner lures (for pike/perch) + floats and hooks for mato-onki (kids).

🇳🇴 Norway (G15–G33)

Norway is every angler's dream: sea fishing is FREE for everyone, no license, no age limits. And the fjords are full of fish.

What to fish (sea): Arctic cod (torsk), pollack (sei), mackerel (makrell), halibut (kveite), coal cod (lyr).

The 5 must-visit spots:

  1. D16 Senja — Husøy and Mefjordvær piers. Cod and pollack. Midnight sun = fishing at 11:00 PM!

  2. D20 Henningsvær — fishing village, piers everywhere. Arctic cod.

  3. D22 Reine — fishing with red rorbu cabins in the background. Iconic.

  4. D27 Atlantic Road — fishing FROM THE BRIDGES over the ocean. Pollack and cod.

  5. D30 Bergen — Bryggen pier, mackerel in July (seasonal peak).

Rules:

Sea/fjord: FREE, no limits (personal use)

Freshwater (rivers/lakes): license required from owner

Salmon/sea trout: mandatory state fee on elveguiden.no + local license

Export: max 15 kg fish per person from 2026 (only if caught at registered tourist facility; self-guided fishing = 0 kg exportable)

Gear: same as Finland works perfectly. For cod from piers: 50-100g sinker + artificial bait (jig) or mackerel fillet.

🇩🇰 Denmark (G33–G39)

Mandatory license (Fisketegn) but easy to get online.

Spots on the route:

🎣 D33 Hirtshals (if you stop): harbor pier — mackerel, cod. Great with kids.

🎣 D36 Billund area: lakes and rivers — trout, pike. Local lake permit also required.

Purchase: fisketegn.dk/en — DKK 46 (~€6.2)/day, DKK 150 (~€20)/week. Kids <18 free.

🇩🇪 Germany (G39–G40)

⚠️ Not recommended. Germany requires an exam (Fischereischein) to fish. Some Länder offer tourist licenses, but Bremen (on your route) is not among them. Skip fishing here — you will have plenty of opportunities before and after.

🇫🇷 France (G40–G42, G50)

Sea: shore fishing FREE, no license (like Italy).

Freshwater: Carte de pêche (~€15/day) required, purchasable at cartedepeche.fr. Kids <12 free.

Spots:

🎣 D42 Loire: Cher river near Chenonceau — pike, perch. Carte de pêche required.

🎣 D50 French Riviera: piers of Antibes, Cannes, Menton — gilthead bream, seabream. FREE.

🇪🇸 Spain (G43–G49)

Sea: ⚠️ Recreational sea fishing license required in all Autonomous Communities (Basque Country, Cantabria, Catalonia). Cost: ~€43/3 years online at fishinglicensespain.com (covers all Spain). Fines without license: €60-600!

Freshwater: additional regional license required (varies by Autonomous Community, ~€10-15/day online).

Spots:

🎣 D43 San Sebastián: harbor pier or Igueldo cliffs — seabream, mackerel.

🎣 D44 Getxo (near Bilbao): old port — sea bass, seabream.

🎣 D45 Picos de Europa: Deva river — brown trout! Cantabria license ~€15/day at medioambientecantabria.es. Many catch & release areas.

🎣 D49 Costa Brava: Cap de Creus, Cadaqués pier — gilthead bream, sea bass.

🇮🇹 Italy (G51–G53)

Sea: shore fishing FREE, no license required.

Spots:

🎣 D52 Genoa: Boccadasse pier or outer breakwater of Porto Antico — white seabream, seabream, mullet.

🎒 Fishing — What to Bring

Gear Use Notes
2.4m telescopic rod + reel Spinning (pike, perch, cod) Compact, fits in van
3-4m fixed rod Mato-onki for kids (float) Cheap, perfect for perch
5-10g spinner lures Finland + Norway Mepps Aglia no.3 = universal
Jigs/sinkers 30-100g Cod from Norwegian piers Weight varies by current
Floats + hooks no.8-12 Kids (worm/bread) Perch, seabream, white seabream
0.25mm line (150m) Universal Nylon or fluorocarbon
Hook remover pliers + scissors Safety Mandatory with kids
Folding bucket Keep fish alive / wash Occupies zero space

🚲 Outdoor Rentals — Bikes, Kayaks, SUP and Scooters

Bring 4 foldable muscle-powered scooters and rent bikes, kayaks or SUP where it makes most sense. This section collects the best opportunities by area.

🛴 Muscle-powered scooters (own)

Muscle scooters are not regulated like electric ones — they are treated as "toys" or equated to pedestrians. No age limit, no mandatory helmet (but recommended for children). In Denmark they ride on the sidewalk; elsewhere also on bike lanes.

Days Location Why ideal Notes
D0-D1 Vienna 🇦🇹 Ringstrasse, Prater, Donauinsel — all flat Excellent bike lanes
D2 Warsaw 🇵🇱 Large pedestrian historic center Vistula riverbank
D4-D5 Riga / Tallinn 🇱🇻🇪🇪 Compact historic centers, seaside promenade Tallinn: Pirita promenade
D9 Oulu 🇫🇮 Bike-friendly city par excellence Top bike lane network in Finland
D20-D23 Lofoten 🇳🇴 Quiet villages, zero traffic Henningsvær, Reine
D26 Trondheim 🇳🇴 Pedestrian center, Bakklandet, waterfront Flat along the fjord
D30 Bergen 🇳🇴 Bryggen and waterfront (flat center) Avoid hills
D34-D38 Copenhagen + Billund 🇩🇰 Very flat, bike lanes everywhere Sidewalk by law
D41-D42 Loire 🇫🇷 Loire à Vélo bike lanes Perfect along the castles
D44 Bilbao 🇪🇸 Pedestrian riverbank up to the Guggenheim Flat
D50-D51 Costa Brava / Côte d'Azur 🇪🇸🇫🇷 Seafronts and seaside promenades Ideal in the evening

Recommended models: large 200mm wheels (like Micro Cruiser or Razor A5 Lux) for children 6-8 years — better on uneven asphalt. For adults: Micro White/Black or Razor A5 Air.

📋 Practical Rental Tips

🎯 Book in advance in high season (July-August) for Lofoten, Geiranger, and Copenhagen

🎯 Kayak with children: prefer sit-on-top or double kayaks; guided tours are safer and include briefing

🎯 Cargo bikes Copenhagen: book online at least 2-3 days ahead, very popular

🎯 Bring: waterproof sunscreen, water shoes, dry bags for phones

🎯 Wet card (Våtkort): required in Norway for self-guided kayak rental without guide — guided tours do not require it

🛸 Drone — Regulations by Country

EASA rules (Open Category) valid across all EU/EEA: max 120m AGL, visual line of sight (VLOS), registration in your home EU country (valid everywhere). Sub-250g drones with camera (e.g. DJI Mini 4 Pro): category C0/A1, no pilot certificate required, can fly near people (not crowds).

Rules by Country — Along the Itinerary

Country Registration Insurance National Parks Key Notes
🇮🇹 Italy Required on D-Flight.it (even sub-250g with camera) ⚠️ Mandatory for all ❌ Prohibited QR code on drone. Banned over historic centers, archaeological sites. Heavy fines.
🇦🇹 Austria EU registration valid ⚠️ Mandatory (specific aviation coverage) ❌ Prohibited (nesting protection) Check dronespace.at before every flight
🇨🇿 Czechia EU registration valid Recommended ⚠️ Check individually Check DroneMap.gov.cz. Banned near Prague Castle.
🇵🇱 Poland EU registration valid Recommended ⚠️ Check individually Generally permissive. Check airport zones.
🇱🇹 Lithuania EU registration valid Recommended ✅ Generally allowed Vilnius old town: restricted. Permissive elsewhere.
🇱🇻 Latvia EU registration valid Recommended ✅ Generally allowed Riga center: restricted. Permissive elsewhere.
🇪🇪 Estonia EU registration valid Recommended ✅ Generally allowed Tallinn old town: restricted. Permissive elsewhere.
🇫🇮 Finland Required on droneinfo.fi (with camera) Recommended ⚠️ Permit required from Metsähallitus Max 150m (higher than EU!). Parks: check specific rules on luontoon.fi
🇳🇴 Norway EU registration valid + register camera with NSM Recommended (>250g mandatory) ❌ Prohibited (Lofotodden NP, reserves) 5km from airports (Svolvær, Leknes!). Check safetofly.no. Severe fines.
🇩🇰 Denmark EU registration valid Recommended ⚠️ Check individually Generally permissive for sub-250g. Copenhagen center: restricted.
🇩🇪 Germany EU registration valid ⚠️ Mandatory for all ❌ Core zones prohibited 100m from motorways/railways. No filming private property without consent.
🇫🇷 France EU registration valid ⚠️ Mandatory ❌ Prohibited Check Géoportail. Many restricted zones.
🇪🇸 Spain EU registration valid ⚠️ Mandatory ❌ Prohibited Check ENAIRE Drones. Beaches: banned in summer.

🎯 Best Drone Spots on the Trip

# Spot Day Why ⚠️ Caution
1 Reine/Hamnøy (Lofoten) D21 Red cabins + mountains. Iconic shot. OUTSIDE Lofotodden National Park! 5km from Leknes airport.
2 Atlantic Ocean Road D27 Spectacular bridges over the ocean. Strong winds common. Check weather.
3 Geirangerfjord D28 UNESCO fjord from above. Distance from cruise ships and waterfalls.
4 Trollstigen D28 Breathtaking serpentine mountain road. Distance from people at viewpoint.
5 Senja (Segla/Husøy) D16 Dramatic coastline, island village. Wind at altitude. No specific restrictions.
6 Punkaharju Ridge (Finland) D7 Ridge between two lakes, boreal forest. Check if protected area.

🎯 Practical Tips

Aspect Detail
Registration Register on D-Flight.it (Italy = home country). Valid across all EU/EEA.
Norway NSM Register camera/sensor with the National Security Authority BEFORE flying in Norway.
Pre-flight apps 🇳🇴 SafeToFly | 🇮🇹 D-Flight | 🇫🇮 Droneinfo.fi | 🇦🇹 Dronespace
Batteries Not relevant for flights (camper trip). In camper: recharge with 12V→220V inverter.
Golden rule ALWAYS check the local app before takeoff. Zones change frequently.

Sources: EASA Drones | SafeToFly.no | Max Haase Drone Rules | D-Flight.it

📡 Garmin inReach — Satellite Coverage & Safety

The Garmin inReach Mini 2 uses the Iridium satellite network (100% global coverage). It’s useful where mobile coverage drops: deep fjords, Arctic mountains, Finnish wilderness. Enables SOS, messaging and tracking even without cell signal.

When to Activate — Critical Zones on the Trip

Zone Days Mobile Coverage Risk Advice
🇳🇴 Lofoten — remote trails (Ryten, Kvalvika, Munkebu) D19–D23 ⚠️ Medium-high (outside villages) Activate for every remote hike
🇳🇴 Senja — Segla, Hesten D16 ⚠️ Medium (valleys without signal) Activate for high-altitude hikes
🇳🇴 Helgelandskysten — remote coast D25–D26 ⚠️ Medium (islands, fjords) Activate if leaving main roads
🇳🇴 Geirangerfjord — deep fjord D28 ⚠️ Medium (cliffs block signal) Useful for hikes outside Geiranger
🇫🇮 Finnish Lapland — wilderness (Inari, Kilpisjärvi) D13–D14 ⚠️ Medium (off main roads) Activate for national park hikes
🇳🇴 Tromsø — Fjellheisen area D15 ✅ Low (city) Not needed in town
🇪🇪🇱🇻🇱🇹 Baltics, 🇵🇱 Poland, 🇨🇿 Czechia D2–D5 ✅ Low (small countries, good coverage) Not needed
🇩🇪 Germany, 🇦🇹 Austria, 🇮🇹 Italy D0–D1, D52–D54 ✅ Low (excellent coverage) Not needed

🎯 Practical Tips

Aspect Detail
Recommended plan Safety (SOS + preset messages) — ~€15/month. Can be activated/suspended month by month.
Activation Activate the plan 1–2 days before departure. Managed at explore.garmin.com
Tracking Set position send every 10 min during hikes. Family can follow on MapShare.
Battery ~14 days standby, ~24h with 10-min tracking. Recharge every evening in camper.
SOS SOS button contacts GEOS (international rescue center). Works anywhere, even without network.
Messages Preset messages like: “All good, back in 2h” / “Delayed, don’t worry”

Sources: Garmin inReach Mini 2 | Garmin Explore | Iridium Coverage

🎫 Tourist Cards — Passes and Discounts by Country

🇳🇴 Norway — AutoPASS / SkyttelPASS (G15–G33)

The Norwegian toll system covers all toll booths, bridges, tunnels, and most internal ferries. For foreign tourists with their own vehicle:

Option Discount Cost How
No registration 0% (invoice at home +20%) — License plate read automatically, invoice sent
SkyttelPASS tag 20% tolls + 10% ferries NOK 200 (~€19) one-time Order 4–6 weeks in advance, shipped home
+ AutoPASS ferje prepayment 50% ferries Deposit NOK 3,600 (~€333) refundable Add after receiving the tag

Estimated trip savings (19 days in Norway): tolls ~NOK 2,500 → 20% discount = ~€43 saved; internal ferries ~NOK 2,000 → 50% discount = ~€87 saved. Total: ~€130 saved (net of tag cost).

⚠️ Warning: the tag must be ordered in advance (postal shipment). The agreement activates 30 minutes after registration (license plate read even without physical tag). The ferje deposit is refundable upon agreement closure.

🔗 skyttelpass.no autopassferje.no autopass.no/en/user/foreign-vehicles

🇩🇰 Denmark — Copenhagen Card DISCOVER (G33–G35)

The Copenhagen Card includes 80+ attractions + unlimited transport in the Capital Region.

Duration Adult (16+) Children (3–11) Family 2+2
24h DKK 589 (~€79) DKK 100 (~€13) ~€186
48h DKK 859 (~€115) DKK 140 (~€19) ~€268
72h DKK 1,039 (~€139) DKK 180 (~€24) ~€330

Included attractions: Tivoli Gardens, Experimentarium, Canal Tour, Rundetårn, Zoo, Rosenborg, Amalienborg, Christiansborg, and 70+ others.

Tip: the 48h (€268 for 4 pax) covers G34–G35 with Tivoli + Experimentarium + canal tour + transport. Without the card these attractions would cost ~€350+. Savings: ~€80+.

⚠️ Legoland and LEGO House (Billund) are NOT included in the Copenhagen Card.

🔗 copenhagencard.com

Other cities (short stay)

For Vienna (G1), Helsinki (G6), Tallinn (G5), Riga (G4), Tromsø (G15), Bergen (G30), Bilbao (G44): the stay is too short (1 day or less) to justify a city card. Buy single tickets for chosen attractions.

⚠️ Logistical Risks — Critical Points

1. "The Baltic Marathon" (G2–G5)

This is the real test of the trip. On paper it seems doable, but in reality it is a stress test for the children:

🚗 D2: Vienna → Warsaw (670 km, 7h 30m)

🚗 D3: Warsaw → Vilnius (470 km, 6h 30m)

🚗 D4: Vilnius → Riga (345 km, 4h 30m)

🚗 D5: Riga → Tallinn (310 km, 4h 30m)

The problem: You will drive over 1,700 km in 4 consecutive days. Considering bathroom breaks, lunches, and traffic, actual travel times will increase by 20-30%. The children will spend most of the time strapped in car seats.

Solution: Always start at dawn (e.g. 5:00 or 6:00 AM). The children will sleep for the first 3-4 hours of travel, allowing you to "cover kilometers" peacefully and arrive at the destination by lunchtime, saving afternoons for parks and explorations.

2. Leaving the Lofoten (G24: Lofoten → Mo i Rana)

The table shows 400 km, 5h + ferry. Be careful as this estimate is optimistic:

The Moskenes–Bodø ferry lasts about 3.5–4 hours

You must be at the boarding at least 1 hour (or 2) before

From Bodø to Mo i Rana there are about 230 km (another 3.5 hours driving)

The problem: This will be a draining day, almost exclusively transit (about 9-10 hours total including driving, waiting, and sailing). Consider it a "lost" day tourist-wise and prepare onboard entertainment for the children.

3. The Ferry Uncertainty (Mandatory Reservations)

The trip relies on some crucial ferries (Tallinn–Helsinki, Moskenes–Bodø, Kristiansand–Hirtshals).

In August and late July, the Moskenes–Bodø route is overwhelmed by motorhome travelers from all over Europe. If you show up at boarding without a reservation, you might have to wait 24 or 48 hours in line (in the "standby lane").

⚠️ You absolutely must book these ferries 2-3 months in advance, which will bind you to strictly follow the schedule up to G24.

The Kristiansand–Hirtshals ferry (G33) is less critical but booking is still recommended in high season.

4. Ferragosto in Genoa (G50–G52)

As noted in the file, the A10 highway at Ferragosto is hell. Being in Genoa on 17/08 (G52) saves you from the absolute peak, but expect very heavy slowdowns in Liguria.

Tip: On 16/08 (G51) from Camargue to Genoa (450 km, A8/A10) — leave at 7:00 AM to avoid the bulk of return traffic. Consider stopping in Savona/Finale Ligure if traffic is blocked.
